Chapter of Retaliation for Injuries Less than Life. It is only in what similarity can be preserved. So the intentional cutter of a hand is retaliated against from the joint. He said 'from the joint' as a precaution for when he cuts from half the forearm or half the shin, for similarity cannot be preserved there. The commentator says: The chapter of retaliation for injuries less than life; when he finished explaining retaliation for life, he began explaining retaliation for less than life because the part follows the whole. His saying 'so he is retaliated against' etc. is because of His statement: 'And wounds are retaliation' (Quran 5:45) meaning they are subject to retaliation because of His statement: 'And the tooth for the tooth'. Retaliation indicates similarity, so the author said: it is only in what similarity can be preserved, meaning everything in which observing similarity is possible requires retaliation, and what does not, does not. On this universal principle he branched rulings, so he said: so he is retaliated against, and similarity is possible in these things we mentioned. When we say similarity, we say size of the limb is not considered because it does not cause difference in benefit, so the criterion is equality in benefit. So the right hand should not be cut for the left, nor the healthy hand for the paralyzed, nor the woman's hand for the man's, nor the free man's hand for the slave's. He restricted his saying 'the cutter of the hand' with 'from the joint' because if he cut from other than the joint, there is no retaliation. So in 'Takmilat al-Bahr'. His saying 'from half the forearm' which is between the elbow and palm. So in 'al-Mughrib'. His saying 'because similarity cannot be preserved' because there is no limit at which the cut ends, so retaliation is not obligatory, but rather an equitable assessment. So in 'al-Bayaniyyah'. And he will explain it in the chapter of diyat. And if his hand is larger than what was cut, like the foot, the tip of the nose, the ear, and the eye when struck and its sight goes while it remains. And if his hand is larger than what was cut like the foot, and the tip of the nose, then the foot if cut from the joint requires retaliation, and the tip of the nose requires retaliation, not the bridge of the nose because similarity cannot be preserved there. And the ear and eye when struck and their sight goes while they remain, then the difference between the two values is the equitable assessment. The commentator says: His saying 'and if his hand is larger than what was cut' means size of hand is not considered because the benefit of the hand does not differ by that, similarly the foot and tip of nose and ear because similarity can be observed in them. His saying 'like the foot' meaning just as the cutter of the foot is retaliated against, and the tip of the nose, which is the soft part separated from the cartilage. So in 'al-Jalabi'. His saying 'tip of the nose' and in 'Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah' from Muhammad: if he cut the tip (the nostril), there is retaliation in it, and if he cut it from its root, no retaliation because it is bone and not a joint, and no retaliation in bone. Abu Hanifa said: if he cut his penis from its root or from the glans, retaliation is inflicted on him because it is possible to exact it in equality as it has a known limit, so it resembles the hand from the wrist. His saying 'and the ear' meaning the cutter of the ear is retaliated against. In 'al-Nawadir', al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: if he cuts the lobe of his ear, he is retaliated against; if he cuts half his ear and can exact similar retaliation, he is retaliated against because the ear lobe has a known limit and the ear has known joints, so if something of it is cut, it is known that cutting from any joint is possible for retaliation. Likewise if he cuts the cartilage of the ear in a way that retaliation is possible, he is retaliated against.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. The author establishes the fundamental principle that qisas (retaliation) for injuries less than life is only obligatory where exact similarity (mumathala) can be preserved. The proof is Allah's statement in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:45): 'And the tooth for the tooth, and wounds are retaliation.' The word 'qisas' itself implies equality. The commentator explains that the restriction 'from the joint' in the case of cutting a hand is to exclude cuts from the middle of the forearm or shin, where no defined limit exists and similarity cannot be maintained. In such cases, the penalty is not qisas but hukumat al-adl (equitable assessment). The principle is universal: wherever similarity is possible, qisas is wajib; where not, it is not. The comment further clarifies that size of the limb is irrelevant for similarity; the criterion is equality in benefit. Thus, the right hand is not taken for the left, nor a healthy hand for a paralyzed one, nor a woman's hand for a man's, nor a free person's hand for a slave's. The foot, ear, and tip of the nose (maran al-anf) are examples where qisas applies because they have defined limits and similarity can be maintained. The bridge of the nose (qasabah) lacks this, so no qisas. For the eye, when sight is lost but the eye remains, qisas is not possible; instead, the difference in value before and after injury is assessed as hukumat al-adl. The text also includes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf from the Nawadir: Imam Muhammad holds that cutting the tip of the nose (nostril) requires qisas, but cutting it from the root (bone) does not because bone has no joint. Abu Hanifa analogizes the penis to the hand: if cut from the root or glans, qisas applies because it has a known limit. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that qisas applies where similarity is possible, following the principle stated.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): Retaliation for bodily injuries less than life, synonymous with qisas.
المماثلة (al-mumathalah): Exact similarity between the injury inflicted and the retaliation.
المفصل (al-mafsil): The natural joint of a limb; the limit from which qisas is possible.
مارن الأنف (maran al-anf): The soft tip of the nose, distinct from the bony bridge; has a defined limit for qisas.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): An equitable monetary assessment when qisas is not possible; the difference in value before and after injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is qisas wajib for a cut to the hand?
A) When the cut is from the joint
B) When the cut is from the forearm
C) When the cut is from the wrist or above
D) When the hand is larger than the cut

Key Takeaway
Qisas for injuries in Hanafi law is wajib only when exact similarity (mumathala) can be preserved; otherwise, the penalty is an equitable monetary assessment (hukumat al-adl).

Qisas — Retaliation

Qisas for Body Parts: Conditions of Similarity
Explains qisas for various body parts with conditions for similarity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on qisas for the hand, foot, nose, ear, eye, and wounds, and explain the condition of exact similarity (mumathalah).

Core Idea
Qisas is wajib only when exact similarity between injury and retaliation is possible.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rules for qisas (retaliation) on various body parts. The key principle is that qisas is only permissible when the harm can be exactly replicated. The passage distinguishes between parts where similarity is possible (e.g., the soft tip of the nose, the ear with known joints) and parts where it is not (e.g., the bony nose, the plucked eye). We will examine the rulings and the proof from the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the body part and applicable ruling
For each body part (hand, foot, nose, ear, eye, wound), determine if qisas is wajib or not based on the text.
The hand and foot: qisas even if sizes differ. Nose: qisas only for the soft tip (maran), not the bone. Ear: qisas if cut at a known joint. Eye: qisas via heated mirror if the eye remains. Wounds: qisas if similarity possible.
2
Apply the mumathalah condition
Assess whether exact replication of the injury is feasible. The maran has a known limit; the bony nose does not. The ear has joints; the torn earlobe does not.
Mumathalah (exact similarity) is the core condition – if impossible, qisas is replaced by compensation (arsh/diyah).
3
Note intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds no qisas for cutting the nose from the root (bone), while Abu Hanifa analogizes it to the penis. For the ear, Abu Hanifa allows qisas for the lobe or half if possible; otherwise arsh.
The mufta bihi follows Zahir al-Riwayah: qisas is possible if exact similarity can be maintained.
4
Examine the proof for the eye method
The heated mirror method is based on the practice of Ali (ra) during Uthman's caliphate. Wet cotton protects the face and other eye.
This is a qawl sahabi (Companion’s ruling) with zanni thubut and dalala, but accepted in the Hanafi school.
5
Analyze the choice when sizes differ
If the offender’s ear is smaller than the victim’s, the victim can choose between half diyah or cutting the smaller ear. If the victim’s ear is deficient, only hukumat adl (just compensation) is due.
This preserves the principle of mumathalah: the retaliation must match the injury as closely as possible.

والأذن والعين إذا ضربت فذهب ضوؤها، وهي قائمة معه ، فقدر التفاوت بين القيمتين هو «باب الديات»: بأن يقوم المجروح بلا هذا الأثر ، ثمّ معا حكومة عدل.

[٤] قوله : والأذن ؛ أي يقتص قاطع الأذن، وفي «النوادر»: روى الحسن له عن أبي حنيفة له : إنه إذا قطع شحمة إذنه يقتص منه، وإن قطع نصف إذنه وكان يقدر أن يقتص مثل ذلك اقتص منه ؛ لأنّ شحمة الإذن لها حدّد معلوم، وللأذن مفاصل معلومة، فإذا قطع شيء منها يعلمُ أنّ القطعَ من أي المفصل أمكن القصاص. وكذلك إذا قطع غضروف الأذن قطعاً يستطاع فيه القصاص، اقتص منه، يعمل فيجعل على وجهه قطن رطب ، ويقابل عينه بمرآة محماة، ولو قلعت لا؛ إذ في القلع لا يمكن رعاية المماثلة.
وكل شجة تراعى فيها المماثلة: كالموضّحة : وهي أن يظهر العظم. ذلك بحديدة أو بغير حديدة، وإن جذب أذنه فانتزعَ شحمته لا قصاص فيه، وعليه الأرش في ماله ، وإن كان إذنُ القاطعُ سَكّا أي صغيرة الخلقة، وإذن المقطوع صحيحة كبيرة، كان بالخيار ؛ إن شاءَ ضمَّنَه نصف الديَّة، وإن شاء قطعها على صغرها. وكذلك لو كانت أذن القاطع مقطوعة أو خرماء أو مشقوقة كان المقطوع بالخيار، وإن كانت الناقصة هي المقطوعة كان له حكومة عدل لا قصاص فيه.
[١] قوله : فيجعل على وجهه ؛ وإنّما احتيج إليه لحفظ الوجه والعين الأخرى التي ليس فيها قصاص ، هذا ما أفاده أخي جلبي.
[٢] قوله : بمرآة محماة ؛ تقرب من عينه حتى يذهب ضوئها، وهو مأخوذ من أحمى الحديد في النار، وهو محمّي ؛ أي جعله في شدة الحرارة. قال في «ردّ المحتار» : المرآة : بكسر الميم ، ومد الهمزة : آلة الرؤية، ورأيت بخط بعض العلماء أن المراد هاهنا قولاً صقيل يرى به الوجه، لا المرأة المعروفة من الزجاج، وهذا ما ذكره المصنف الله مأثور عن الصحابة ، كما قال صاحب «الهداية». وفي «الزَّيْلَعِي : كانت هذه الحادثة وقعت في زمن عثمان ، فشاوروا الصحابة له ، فقال علي : يجب القصاص ، فبين إمكانه بالطريق الذي ذكرناه.

And if his hand is larger than what he cut, like the foot, and the soft tip of the nose, and the ear, and the eye when struck while intact and its light (vision) goes, and it (says: And if his hand is larger than what he cut, like the foot) and the soft tip of the nose. Indeed, the foot when cut from the joint requires qisas, and in the soft tip of the nose qisas is required, not in the nasal bone, because exact similarity cannot be preserved there. And the ear and the eye when struck and its light (vision) goes while it remains with him, then the measure of the difference between the two values is from 'Chapter of Diyat': that the injured person be evaluated without this effect, then with it, and a just assessment. [1] His saying: And if his hand is larger than what he cut, means that the largeness or smallness of the hand is not considered, because the benefit of the hand does not differ with that; similarly the foot and the soft tip of the nose and the ear, because it is possible to maintain similarity in them. [2] His saying: like the foot, meaning just as the cutter of the foot is subject to qisas, and the soft tip of the nose, which is what is soft and separates from the bone. This is in al-Jalabi. [3] His saying: the soft tip of the nose; and in the Nawadir of Ibn Sama'ah: from Muhammad: if he cuts the soft tip, which is the tip of the nose, then there is qisas in it; if he cuts from its root, no qisas on him because it is bone and not a joint, and there is no qisas in bone. And Abu Hanifa said: If he cuts his penis from its root or from the glans, qisas is applied on him, because it is possible to exact it on the basis of equality, since it has a known limit, so it resembles the hand from the wrist. [4] His saying: the ear, meaning the cutter of the ear is subject to qisas. And in al-Nawadir: al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if he cuts his earlobe, qisas is applied on him; if he cuts half his ear and it is possible to cut the like of it, qisas is applied on him, because the earlobe has a known limit, and the ear has known joints; so if something of it is cut, it is known from which joint the cutting was possible for qisas. Similarly, if he cuts the cartilage of the ear in a way that qisas is possible, qisas is applied on him. He acts: he places on his face wet cotton, and he brings near his eye a heated mirror; but if it is plucked out, no qisas, because similarity cannot be maintained. And every wound where similarity is considered, like the al-muddihah: where the bone appears. That is with an iron tool or without a tool. If he pulled his ear and tore off his earlobe, no qisas in it, and he must pay the compensatory value (arsh) from his wealth. And if the ear of the cutter is small (in creation), and the ear of the victim is healthy and large, then he has a choice: if he wishes, he can hold him liable for half the diyah, and if he wishes, he can cut it according to its smallness. Similarly, if the ear of the cutter is cut, or pierced, or slit, the victim has a choice. And if the deficient one is the victim's ear, then he is entitled to a just assessment (hukumat adl) and no qisas in it. [1] His saying: he places on his face; it is needed to protect the face and the other eye in which there is no qisas. This is what my brother Jalabi indicated. [2] His saying: with a heated mirror; it is brought near his eye until its light vanishes. This is taken from heating iron in fire, and it is heated, meaning he made it extremely hot. He said in Radd al-Muhtar: al-mirat (mirror) is with kasra of the meem and madd of the hamza: an instrument of seeing. I saw in the handwriting of some scholars that what is meant here is a polished substance by which the face is seen, not the well-known woman (i.e., mirror) of glass. This is what the author narrated as transmitted from the Companions, as the author of al-Hidayah said. And in al-Zaylai: This incident occurred in the time of Uthman, and they consulted the Companions, and Ali said: Qisas is obligatory, so he explained its possibility by the method we mentioned. [3] His saying: every wound; it is conjunctive to the foot. Know that smallness and largeness are not considered in the previous issue, so qisas is applied in all; and it is considered regarding head wounds when they are...

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings on qisas (retaliation) for various body parts from the book of crimes (kitab al-jinayat) in Hanafi fiqh. The commentator explains that for the hand, foot, soft tip of the nose (maran al-anf), ear, and eye, qisas is obligatory when exact similarity can be maintained. For the hand and foot, size differences are ignored because the function is the same. For the nose, qisas applies only to the soft part (maran), not the bony bridge (qasaba), because similarity is impossible with bone. The ear and eye have special rulings: the ear has known joints, so precise cutting is possible; the eye, when struck but not removed, can be subjected to qisas by bringing a heated mirror near it to replicate the harm—a method traced back to a ruling by Ali during Uthman's caliphate. If the ear is torn off, only compensation (arsh) is due. When the offender's ear is smaller than the victim's, the victim may choose between taking half the full diyah or cutting the offender's small ear. Finally, wounds (shijaj) like al-muddihah (where the bone appears) also allow qisas if similarity is feasible.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily injury or killing, when exact similarity is possible.
مارن الأنف (maran al-anf): The soft, fleshy tip of the nose that separates from the nasal bone.
شجة (shajjah): A wound on the head or face that exposes the bone (al-muddihah) or lesser.
موضحة (muddihah): A wound that exposes the bone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qisas for bodily injuries is restricted to cases where exact similarity (mumathalah) can be achieved, as demonstrated by the rulings on the hand, foot, nose, ear, eye, and head wounds.

Ruling on Qisas for Ear Mutilation When Sizes Differ
Ruling on qisas for ear when attacker's ear is smaller or deficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for ear injuries when the ears differ in size or condition, and explain the victim's options.

Core Idea
For ear qisas, the victim may choose compensation or qisas even if the perpetrator's ear is smaller, but not if the victim's ear is deficient.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi criminal law: what happens when the ears of the victim and perpetrator are not identical? The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that the victim retains a powerful choice, even when the perpetrator's ear is smaller or defective, but that choice is limited if the victim's own ear is deficient. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the conditions that trigger or block qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling for removal of fatty tissue
The passage first rules on pulling the ear and removing its fatty part (shahmah). Note that there is no qisas for this; instead, the offender pays arsh (compensation). This establishes a baseline: qisas requires cutting the ear itself, not just its fat.
2
Analyze the scenario when ears differ in size
Next, consider the case where the cutter's ear is small (sakk) and the victim's ear is large and healthy. The passage states that the victim has an option: either demand half the diyah (compensation) or perform qisas on the small ear. Understand that size difference does not prevent qisas.
The ear is a limb with a clear boundary; qisas is based on the act of cutting, not cosmetic matching.
3
Examine when the cutter's ear is deficient
The passage extends the option to cases where the cutter's ear is already cut, pierced, or split. The victim may still choose qisas or compensation. This reinforces the principle that the perpetrator's defect does not block qisas.
4
Identify the blocked scenario: victim's ear is deficient
Finally, the passage states that if the victim's ear is the deficient one, there is no qisas. Instead, the victim receives hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation). This is the key exception: qisas is only available when the victim's limb is intact.
The prevention is due to the impossibility of exact retaliation (the cut would not mirror the injury).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن جذب أذنه فانتزعَ شحمته لا قصاص فيه، وعليه الأرش في ماله ، وإن كان إذنُ القاطعُ سَكّا أي صغيرة الخلقة، وإذن المقطوع صحيحة كبيرة، كان بالخيار ؛ إن شاءَ ضمَّنَه نصف الديَّة، وإن شاء قطعها على صغرها. وكذلك لو كانت أذن القاطع مقطوعة أو خرماء أو مشقوقة كان المقطوع بالخيار، وإن كانت الناقصة هي المقطوعة كان له حكومة عدل لا قصاص فيه).
And if he pulled his ear and removed its fatty part, there is no qisas for it, and he must pay the arsh from his wealth. If the ear of the cutter is a sikka, i.e., small in form, and the ear of the victim is healthy and large, the victim has the option: if he wishes, he can hold him liable for half the diyah, and if he wishes, he can cut it (the cutter's ear) despite its smallness. Similarly, if the cutter's ear is already cut, or has a hole, or is split, the victim has the option. If the deficient ear belongs to the victim, then he receives a just compensation (hukumat 'adl), and there is no qisas.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on qisas for ear mutilation when the ears differ in size or condition. The passage type is a ruling_statement with conditions. The author first states the general rule: if someone pulls another's ear and removes its fatty part (shahmah), there is no qisas because exact similarity is impossible; instead, the offender pays arsh (compensation for the wound). However, if the ear is completely cut off, qisas may apply. The key issue here is when the ears of the two parties are not identical. If the cutter's ear is small (sikka) and the victim's ear is large and healthy, the victim has a choice: either demand half the diyah (full blood money for an ear is half the full diyah, i.e., 500 dinars or 5000 dirhams) or insist on qisas by cutting the small ear. Although the small ear does not match the large one in size, similarity is not required in this case because the ear is a limb with a specific boundary; qisas is applied based on the act of cutting, not on cosmetic matching. Conversely, if the cutter's ear is already deficient (cut, pierced, or split), the victim still has the option to take qisas from the deficient ear or take compensation. But if the victim's own ear is the deficient one, then qisas is not possible, and he receives hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation assessed by experts), not the full arsh of a healthy ear. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that in bodily injuries, qisas is primarily about the action, not the resulting shape, but impossibility of equality prevents qisas.

Key Terms
الأرش (al-arsh): Compensation for injury measured by the reduction in value of the limb, assessed by experts.
سَكّ (sakk): Here it means small in size, literally 'a small ear'.
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): An equitable compensation determined by a judge based on the extent of the injury, not a fixed amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only qisas is available
C) The victim may choose between half diyah or qisas on the small ear
D) The victim must accept hukumat 'adl

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, for ear mutilation, the victim may choose qisas or compensation even if the perpetrator's ear is smaller or deficient, but not if the victim's own ear is deficient.

No Qisas for Bone Except Teeth
Ruling with proof on qisas for bone and teeth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for bone injuries, explain the exception for teeth, and describe the method of retaliation (filing) for broken or pulled teeth.

Core Idea
Qisas is not for bones, but teeth are an exception because precise filing is possible.

The passage establishes a key principle in Hanafi criminal law: retaliation (qisas) for physical injury requires exact equality. Since bones are difficult to equalize, qisas is generally not applicable. However, teeth are treated as an exception because they can be filed to match the injury. This ruling is supported by statements of the Companions Umar and Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Note the clear statement: 'No qisas in bone except in the tooth.' This means the default rule is that bone injuries do not qualify for qisas.
The Arabic phrase is 'لا قود في عظم إلا في السن'.
2
Recognize the exception and its basis
The exception for teeth requires that a tooth be considered bone. The Hanafi school holds that a tooth is bone, making the exception 'connected' (istithna' muttasil). If tooth were not bone, the exception would be disconnected and qisas would not apply.
There is a medical dispute mentioned, but the Hanafi position is that it is bone.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is from the sayings of Umar and Ibn Abbas, transmitted by Ibn Abi Shayba. Umar said: 'We do not execute qisas for bones,' and Ibn Abbas said: 'There is no qisas in bones.' These are qawl sahabi, which is a source of law according to Hanafis.
The dalil is zanni in transmission and meaning.
4
Apply the ruling to two scenarios
If a tooth is broken, the offender's tooth is filed to match the break. If a tooth is pulled out, the offender's tooth is not pulled but filed down to the flesh. This is the mufta bihi position.
Pulling is avoided because exact equality is difficult and could damage the second tooth.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For pulling out, al-Quduri holds that the offender's tooth is filed, not pulled. Al-Sarakhsi prefers this view. A minority narration allows pulling, but it is not the relied-upon position.
The tarjih authority is Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi.

ولا قود في عظم إلا في السن. قوله : ولا قود الخ؛ قال عمر : إنا لا نقيد من العظام، وقال ابن عباس : ليس في العظام قصاص، ونحوه عن الشعبي والحسن ، رواه ابن شيبة في «مصنفه». كذا في «شرح النقاية». قوله : إلا في السن؛ أي إن كان السن عظماً ، فاستثناء : إلا؛ متصل، ولا بدّ من فرق بينها وبين غيرها من العظام، وهو إمكان القصاص فيها، بأن برد السن بالمبرد بقدر ما كسر منها، أو إلى أصلها، فإن قلعها ولا يقلع لتعدّر المماثلة، فربّما يفسد به الثانية. كذا في «المبسوط». وإن كان غير عظم فالاستثناء منقطع ، وقد اختلف الأطباء في ذلك : فمنهم من قال هو طرف عصب يابس؛ لأنه يحدث وينمو بعد تمام الخلقة، ومنهم من قال هو طرف عظم، ثمّ تحقيق المقام على ما في تكملة البحر»: إنه إذا قلع رجل سن غيره، هل يقلع سنّه قصاصاً أم يبرد بالمبرد إلى أن ينتهي إلى اللحم؟ فيه روايتان كما أفصح عنه في «المحيط البرهاني» حيث قال: إن كانت الجناية بكسر بعض السن يؤخذ من سن الكاسر بالمبرد مقدار ما كسر من سنّ الآخر، وهذا بالاتفاق، وإن كانت الجنايةُ بقطع سن ذَكَرَ القُدُوري أنه لا يقلع سن القالع، ولكن يبرد سن القالع بالمبرد إلى أن ينتهي إلى اللحم، ويسقط الباقي، وإليه مال شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسِي
And no qisas in bone except in the tooth. His saying: 'No qisas etc.'; Umar said: 'We do not execute qisas for bones,' and Ibn Abbas said: 'There is no qisas in bones,' and similar from al-Sha'bi and al-Hasan, reported by Ibn Abi Shayba in his Musannaf. This is from Sharh al-Niqaya. His saying: 'except in the tooth'; meaning if the tooth is bone, then the exception 'except' is connected (ittisal). There must be a difference between it and other bones, and that is the possibility of qisas in it, by filing the tooth with a file to the extent that was broken, or to its root. If it was pulled out, then the tooth of the offender should not be pulled out because similarity is difficult; perhaps it would spoil the second tooth. This is from al-Mabsut. If (the tooth) is not bone, then the exception is disconnected (munqati'). The physicians have differed in this: some say it is a dry nerve end because it grows after full creation, and some say it is a piece of bone. Then the investigation of the matter according to Takmilat al-Bahr: if a man pulls out another's tooth, should his tooth be pulled out as qisas, or should it be filed with a file until it reaches the flesh? There are two narrations as clarified in al-Muhit al-Burhani where he said: If the injury is by breaking part of a tooth, then from the tooth of the breaker, a file is used to take the amount equal to what was broken of the other's tooth, and this is by agreement. If the injury is by cutting (pulling out) a tooth, al-Quduri mentioned that the tooth of the puller is not pulled out, but rather the tooth of the puller is filed with a file until it reaches the flesh, and the rest is left. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi inclined to this.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on qisas for bone injuries, with the exception of teeth. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as it quotes narrations from Umar and Ibn Abbas establishing the general rule. The matn states clearly: 'No qisas in bone except in the tooth.' The commentary explains that teeth are an exception because exact similarity is possible through filing. If a tooth is broken, the offender's tooth can be filed to match the extent of the break. If a tooth is completely pulled out, the Hanafi position (according to al-Quduri and al-Sarakhsi) is not to pull out the offender's tooth, but to file it down to the flesh, leaving the rest, because pulling might cause damage to the second tooth. The passage also notes a medical dispute: whether the tooth is bone or a nerve. If it is bone, the exception is connected (mustathna muttasil); if not, the exception is disconnected (munqati'), meaning the rule of no qisas applies. The Hanafi school adopts the view that it is bone, and thus qisas is applicable. The ruling reflects careful consideration of practical feasibility and prevention of excessive harm.

Key Terms
قود (qawad/qisas): Retaliation in kind for physical injury.
السن (al-sinn): Tooth, exempted from the general rule of no qisas in bone.
استثناء متصل (istithna' muttasil): Connected exception, meaning the exception belongs to the same category as the general rule (tooth is bone).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The offender's tooth is filed to match the break.
C) Only monetary compensation is given.

Key Takeaway
Qisas for bone injuries is limited to teeth, and the method is filing, not pulling, to ensure precise equality and avoid excessive harm.

No Qisas for Half Forearm or Healed Ja'ifah
Ruling on no qisas for half forearm cut and healed ja'ifah with proof and objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for a half forearm cut and a healed ja'ifah, explain the requirement of exact equivalence (mumathala), and evaluate the response to the absolute Quranic verse.

Core Idea
No qisas without exact equivalence; limbs are treated like property, not life.

In Hanafi law, qisas for limbs requires precise equivalence (mumathala) in both value and anatomical location. When such equivalence is impossible—as in cutting from half the forearm or a healed wound reaching the body cavity—qisas is not applicable. This lesson examines the ruling, its basis in treating limbs as property, and the Hanafi response to the Quranic verse 'Eye for an eye' that opponents cite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the ruling
The passage rules that there is no qisas for cutting a hand from half the forearm and for a ja'ifah (body-cavity wound) that has healed. Determine what each act is and the legal consequence.
2
Understand the rationale: limbs as property
The author states that limbs are treated like property (amwal), so qisas requires exact equivalence. If the value or location cannot be matched precisely, qisas is invalid. Grasp the principle that mumathala is a condition.
3
Analyze the proof: Quranic verse and objection
Opponents cite Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45, which seems absolute. The Hanafi response explains that the verse has been partially specified by consensus (e.g., harbi and musta'min), and once partially specified, the remainder can be specified by a solitary hadith. Trace this argument.
4
Apply the specification principle
The Hanafi school relies on a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) to specify the absolute text. Confirm that specification by ahad hadith is permissible in Hanafi usul after consensus has established a precedent of specification.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Because qisas is negated, compensation (diyah) becomes the default remedy. Note the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi and opposing views.

We say: It has been specified regarding the harbi and the musta'min by consensus, and when something is specified from an absolute text, it is permissible to specify the rest by a solitary report, as established in usul, so we specified it by what we have narrated. This is in al-Kifayah.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The author states the Hanafi rule: there is no qisas for cutting a hand from half the forearm because there is no defined joint to ensure exact equivalence, and no qisas for a ja'ifah (a wound reaching the body cavity) that has healed because precise matching is impossible. Limbs are treated like property, and qisas requires exact equivalence (mumathala) in value and location. The objection from the Quranic verse 'The eye for the eye...' is answered by noting that the verse has been specified by consensus for certain cases (harbi and musta'min), and specification by a solitary hadith is valid. Thus the Hanafi position is based on the principle that absolute texts can be further specified.

No Qisas Between Slaves of Equal Value Due to Estimation
Objection about slave cutting slave's hand and Hanafi response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas between slaves when their values are equal and explain why estimation (hazr wa zann) prevents the required certainty.

Core Idea
Qisas requires certainty in equivalence; value by estimation is too uncertain to justify qisas between slaves.

This passage presents a common objection to the Hanafi position: if a slave cuts the hand of another slave and their market values are equal, why is qisas not applied? The Hanafi response is that a slave's value is determined by estimation and conjecture, which lack the certainty required for the equivalence (mumathala) necessary for qisas. Understanding this rational proof deepens our grasp of how the Hanafi school prioritizes epistemic certainty in penal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being considered? A slave cutting the hand of another slave. What is the ruling? Qisas does not apply, even if values are equal.
The act falls under jinayat (injuries) and qisas (retaliation).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the value of a slave is known through hazr wa zann (estimation and conjecture), which are inherently uncertain.
No direct textual proof from Quran or Sunnah is cited; the argument is based on the nature of valuation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Qisas requires mumathala (equivalence) between the victim and the offender. For slaves, equivalence is in terms of monetary value. Since value is estimated, equality cannot be established with certainty. Therefore, qisas cannot be imposed.
The certainty required is qat'i; hazr wa zann is zanni, insufficient for penal consequences.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf (disagreement) and tarjih (preference)
Opponents might argue that apparent equality of value suffices. The Hanafi response is that conjecture does not provide the required epistemic standard. The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi ruling.
The tarjih rests on the principle that penal liability demands certainty (shubhat al-'uqūbāt daf' bi al-shubuhāt).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : يشكل بما إذا قطع عبد يد عبد، وقيمتهما سواء، ومع ذلك لا يجري القصاص عندكم. قلنا : لأنَّ طريق معرفة القيمة بالحزر والظنّ، والمماثلة المشروطة لا يثبت بطريق الظن والحزر.
If it is said: It is problematic when a slave cuts the hand of a slave, and their values are equal, yet qisas does not apply according to you. We say: Because the method of knowing value is by estimation and conjecture, and the required equivalence is not established by conjecture and estimation.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and the Hanafi response. The objector asks: if a slave cuts the hand of another slave, and the two slaves are of equal market value, why is qisas not applied? The Hanafi response is that the value of a slave is determined by estimation (hazr) and conjecture (zann), which are imprecise. The required equivalence (mumathala) for qisas must be established with certainty, not through guesswork. Therefore, qisas is not wajib even if values appear equal, because the appearance of equality is not certain.

Key Terms
الحزر والظن (al-hazr wa al-zann): Estimation and conjecture; methods used to determine market value of slaves.
المماثلة المشروطة (al-mumathalah al-mashrutah): The required equivalence in value for qisas.

Qisas for Tongue and Penis: The Glans Exception
Ruling on qisas for tongue and penis with exception for glans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for cutting the tongue and penis, identify the exception for the glans, and explain the reasoning based on the principle of mumathala.

Core Idea
Qisas for tongue and penis is wajib only when the cut is at a defined limit like the glans, due to difficulty in ensuring equality.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah comments on the ruling of qisas (retaliation) for cutting the tongue or penis. The Hanafi school makes an important exception: qisas is not required for cutting the entire organ, but only if the cut is precisely at the glans of the penis or a similarly defined boundary. The reasoning hinges on the principle of exact similarity (mumathalah) — since the tongue and penis contract and expand, equality cannot be guaranteed. Learn the rule, its proof, and the disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its General Ruling
The passage states that for cutting the tongue or the entire penis, qisas is not wajib. Recognize this as the base ruling with the exception of the glans.
The exception is phrased as 'except if the glans is cut'.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is given: 'because contraction and expansion occur in them, so similarity is not considered'. Understand that the inability to ensure exact equivalence prevents qisas.
The proof is based on the principle of mumathalah (equality).
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that if the cut is from the base of the penis, qisas applies. Contrast this with the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad that only the glans qualifies.
This disagreement is about what constitutes a 'defined limit'.
4
Understand the Exception for the Glans
The glans is considered a known limit like a joint, so cutting it makes qisas wajib. Cutting part of the glans or part of the penis (without a defined limit) does not trigger qisas.
The ear and lip are discussed as contrasts: they have fixed limits and do not contract, so qisas applies for cuts.
5
Apply the Ruling to New Cases
Use the principle to determine qisas for other body parts: if the part has a known limit and does not change shape, qisas may apply; otherwise, only compensation (arsh) is due.
This step requires analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واللسان والذكر إلا أن يقطع الحشفة. ( واللّسانِ والذكر إلا أن يقطع الحشفة)، هذا عندنا ; لأن الانقباض والانبساط يجري فيهما فلا تراعى المماثلة، وعن أبي يوسف له : إن كان القطع من الأصل يقتص.
[١]قوله : إلا أن يقطع الحشفة ; أي يجب القصاص إن قطع الحشفة ; لأنّ موضعَ القطع معلوم كالمفصل، ولو قطع بعض الحشفة أو بعض الذكر فلا قصاص فيه ; لأنّ البعض لا يعلم مقداره بخلاف الإذن إذا قطع كلّه أو بعضه; لأنه لا ينقبض ولا ينبسط , ولـه حـد معلوم , فيمكن اعتبار المساواة، والشفّةُ إذا قطعت كلّهـا يجـب القـصـاص ; لإمكان اعتبار المساواة بخلاف قطع البعض ; لأنه يتعذر اعتبارها.
And the tongue and the penis except if the glans is cut. (The tongue and the penis except if the glans is cut), this is according to us because contraction and expansion occur in them so similarity is not considered. And from Abu Yusuf: if the cut is from the base, qisas is applied. [1] His statement: 'except if the glans is cut' means qisas is obligatory if the glans is cut because the place of cutting is known like a joint. If he cuts part of the glans or part of the penis, there is no qisas because the part is not known in measure, unlike the ear if cut entirely or partially because it does not contract or expand, and has a known limit, so equality can be considered. The lip if cut entirely, qisas is obligatory because equality is possible, contrary to cutting part of it because equality is impossible.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of qisas for cutting the tongue and the penis. The Hanafi position is that qisas is not obligatory for cutting the entire tongue or penis unless the cut is exactly at the glans (for the penis) or a similarly defined limit. The reason is that these organs contract and expand, making it difficult to ensure exact equality (mumathala). However, if the cut is at the glans, which has a known limit like a joint, qisas becomes wajib. Abu Yusuf holds that if the cut is from the base, qisas is also applied. The super-commentary elaborates that cutting part of the glans or part of the penis without a defined limit does not warrant qisas, unlike the ear or lip, which have fixed boundaries and do not contract, so qisas applies for the whole or part. This ruling is based on the principle of maintaining exact equivalence in qisas.

Key Terms
الحشفة (al-hashafah): The glans of the penis; a defined part with a known limit like a joint.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for bodily harm, specifically the cutting of the same limb.
المماثلة (al-mumathalah): Equality or similarity between the injury inflicted and the retaliation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits qisas for tongue and penis to cuts at defined parts like the glans to ensure exact equivalence.

Equality of Muslim and Dhimmi in Qisas for Limbs
Ruling that Muslim and dhimmi limbs are equal for qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qisas for limbs between a Muslim and a dhimmi and apply it to a hypothetical injury case.

Core Idea
A Muslim and a dhimmi are equal in qisas for limbs — no distinction in value or obligation.

This lesson presents a foundational Hanafi principle: in the law of qisas (retaliation) for limbs, a Muslim and a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim) are treated identically. This reflects the full legal protection granted to dhimmis in the Islamic state. The same equality applies to inheritance, as noted in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The act is qisas (retaliation) for a limb (e.g., hand, foot, finger). What is the ruling? It is obligatory (wajib) when a limb is injured intentionally and unjustly.
The text says 'wajib al-qisas' implicitly through the word 'sawa' (equal), meaning the obligation applies equally.
2
Identify the parties
Who are the parties? A Muslim and a dhimmi. The ruling states they are equal, meaning the same qisas applies whether the victim is Muslim or dhimmi, and whether the perpetrator is Muslim or dhimmi.
This rule is based on the general protection (dhimma) granted to non-Muslim subjects.
3
Understand the basis
Why are they equal? The text does not give a proof (dalil) but implies it is based on the principle of equality in human dignity and legal protection. In Hanafi usul, the limb of a dhimmi is fully protected like that of a Muslim.
The commentary also mentions equality in inheritance, suggesting a broader principle of equal treatment in certain legal matters.
4
Note the scope and adjacent rulings
Does this cover all types of injuries? The ruling is explicitly for limbs (al-atraf), not necessarily for life or other harms. For life, the Hanafi school also holds a Muslim is killed for a dhimmi (though other schools differ).
The text also mentions equality in inheritance, showing another area of equal treatment.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a case: A Muslim cuts off the finger of a dhimmi intentionally. According to this ruling, the Muslim's finger may be cut in retaliation (qisas) if conditions of equality and intentionality are met.
Practical consequence: No discrimination in criminal retaliation based on religion in Hanafi law.

Source Text

And the limb of a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal. [2] His statement 'equal' means qisas is obligatory in limbs between Muslim and disbeliever; they are equal in inheritance.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage states a basic Hanafi principle: in qisas for limbs, a Muslim and a dhimmi (non-Muslim protected subject) are treated equally. The brief commentary explains that this equality also extends to inheritance (irth). The ruling is straightforward and does not require proof in this text, but it is based on the general principle of protection of life and limb for all citizens of the Islamic state.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of the Islamic state.
الأطراف (al-atraf): Limbs or extremities; in context, body parts subject to qisas.

Victim's Choice When Aggressor's Limb is Defective
Ruling on victim's option in qisas when exact equivalence is impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the victim's choice when exact qisas is impossible due to a defective limb, and apply the choice to scenarios involving paralyzed hands or mismatched head wounds.

Core Idea
When exact qisas is impossible, the victim may choose between defective qisas and full compensation (arsh).

In Hanafi criminal law, qisas (retaliation) requires exact equivalence. But what happens if the aggressor's limb is defective—for example, paralyzed or missing a finger? This lesson examines the ruling from the Hanafi school, which grants the victim a choice: either take the defective limb in qisas or demand full financial compensation (arsh). The principle is based on the impossibility of exacting the right fully, as explained by the classical authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of impossibility
Determine if the aggressor's limb is defective (e.g., paralyzed, missing finger) or if the head wound sizes are mismatched. This creates a situation where exact equivalence is impossible.
The key condition is that exact equivalence is unattainable.
2
State the default rule for qisas
Qisas requires exact equivalence; if that is impossible, the ruling changes from mandatory retaliation to a choice.
This is based on the principle that the right cannot be exacted fully.
3
Present the Hanafi ruling of choice
The victim has the right (khayar) to either take the defective limb in qisas (imperfect retaliation) or demand full arsh (compensation). The victim is not forced to accept the defective limb alone.
The text says: 'he is given the choice: if he wishes, he cuts the defective hand, and if he wishes, he takes the full compensation.'
4
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The proof is rational: because exacting fully is impossible (muta'adhdhir), the victim may either forgive without full right or switch to compensation. This is analogized to fungible goods when none remain.
The analogy shows that when exact replacement is impossible, the creditor may take the available item or demand value.
5
Apply to head wound cases
If the victim's head wound is larger than the aggressor's, qisas is initially allowed if fatal, but the victim has a choice if it heals. If the aggressor's wound is smaller, the victim also has a choice because exacting would exceed the right.
Al-Hidayah confirms the same principle in the opposite case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخير المجني عليه إن كانت يد القاطع شلاء، أو ناقصة بأصبع، أو الشجةُ لا تستوعب ما بينَ قرني الساج، واستوعب ما بين قرني المشجوج يجري فيها القصاص ; لأنَّ البرء فيها نادر , فالظاهرُ أَنَّ الثَّاني يفضي إلى الهلاك , أما إذا لم تبرأ , فإن كانت سارية يجب القصاص، فإن لم تسر بَعْدُ لا يقتص إلى أن يظهر الحال من البرء والسراية. [٣] قوله وخير ; على صيغة المجهول ; أي خُيّر المجني عليه إن شاء قطع اليد المعيبة، ولا شيء له غير اليد المعيبة، وإن شاء أخذ الأرش كاملاً ; لأنَّ استيفاء الحق كاملاً مُتَعَذِّرٌ , فله أن يعفو بدون حقه، وله أن يعدل إلى العوض، كالمثلي إذا لم يبق منه. والرأس المشجوج صغير استوعب الشَّجَةِ ما بين قرنيه، ورأس الشاج عظيم لا تستوعب الشجة وهي شبر ما بين قرنيه فالشَّبرُ الذي لحق المشجوجَ أكثر مما يلحق الشاج، فالمشجرج بالخيار إن شاءَ اقتص، وإن شاء أخذ الأرش. [1] قوله : والرأس المشجوج ... الخ ; قال في «الهداية»(۲) : وفي عكسه يُخَيَّرُ أيضاً ; لانه يتعدَّرُ الاستيفاء كملاً للتعدّي إلى غير حقه، وكذا إذا كانت الشجة في طول الرأس وهي تأخذ من جبهته إلى قفاه، ولا تبلغ إلى قفا الشاج، فهو بالخيار ; لأن المعنى لا يختلف.
And the victim is given a choice if the hand of the cutter is paralyzed, or deficient by a finger, or the head wound does not cover between the two horns of the saj (the wound's boundaries), and it covers between the horns of the wounded person, then qisas is carried out because healing is rare, so it appears that the second leads to death. But if it does not heal, if it spreads, qisas is obligatory; if it has not yet spread, qisas is not carried out until the situation of healing and spread becomes clear. [3] His statement 'and he is given a choice' in the passive form means the victim is given the choice: if he wishes, he cuts the defective hand and nothing else for him except the defective hand; if he wishes, he takes the full compensation (arsh) because full exacting of the right is impossible. So he may forgive without his right, or he may switch to compensation, like the case of a fungible good when none remains. And the head of the wounded person is small, the wound covers between his horns, and the head of the striker is large, the wound does not cover between his horns, and it is a span between his horns, so the span that struck the wounded is more than what strikes the striker, so the wounded has the choice: if he wishes, he exacts qisas, and if he wishes, he takes the compensation. [1] His statement: 'And the head of the wounded...' etc. He said in Al-Hidayah: and in its opposite, he also has a choice because exacting fully is impossible due to exceeding beyond his right. Likewise, if the wound is along the length of the head taking from his forehead to his nape, and it does not reach the nape of the striker, he has a choice because the meaning does not differ.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where exact qisas is impossible due to a defect in the aggressor's limb or a disparity in wound sizes. The Hanafi ruling gives the victim a choice: either take the defective limb (imperfect qisas) or demand full compensation (arsh). The text provides examples: if the aggressor's hand is paralyzed (shalla) or missing a finger, or if the head wound on the victim is larger than what can be inflicted on the aggressor, then exact equality is impossible. In the case of head wounds, if the victim's wound is larger, qisas is initially carried out if it is likely fatal, but if it heals without spreading, the victim may choose. The commentary from Al-Hidayah adds that in the opposite case (aggressor's wound smaller), the victim also has a choice because exacting would exceed his right. This ruling is based on the principle that qisas requires exact equivalence, and when that is impossible, the victim has a compensatory option.

Key Terms
شلاء (shalla'): Paralyzed or crippled, referring to a non-functioning hand.
أرش (arsh): Financial compensation for bodily injury, a fixed sum depending on the injury.
شجة (shajjah): A head wound; specifically, a wound that reaches the bone.

Dropping of Qisas by Death, Pardon, or Settlement
Ruling that qisas is dropped by killer's death, heirs' pardon, or settlement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three ways qisas is dropped in Hanafi fiqh and identify the primary textual proofs from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Qisas is dropped by killer's death, heirs' pardon, or any settlement — no fixed amount required.

What happens to the right of qisas when the killer dies, the heirs forgive, or they agree on compensation? This lesson examines three clear avenues for dropping qisas under Hanafi law, supported by Quranic verse and prophetic practice. Understanding these options reveals the school's emphasis on reconciliation and the discretionary nature of the heirs' right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three ways qisas is dropped
The passage explicitly lists: (1) death of the killer, (2) pardon by the legal heirs, and (3) a settlement (sulh) on any amount of wealth, little or much.
These are exhaustive — no other method (e.g., repentance) drops qisas.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites Quran 2:178 (فَمَنْ عُنِى لَهُ مِنْ أَخِيهِ شَيْءٌ) and a hadith giving heirs the choice between qisas and blood-money.
The Quranic phrase ‘granted something by his brother’ is interpreted as pardon or settlement.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning
Qisas is a right of the heirs (ḥaq thābit lil-wurathā). Therefore, they may drop it by pardon or accept compensation by mutual consent. The amount is not fixed by sacred text, so any agreed sum suffices.
The rationale includes kindness to the killer and preservation of life.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafiʿi) require the settlement amount to be at least the prescribed diyah, arguing that a smaller amount may be unjust. The Hanafi school rejects this limitation due to absence of a textual restriction.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is preferred because the texts do not specify a minimum; the heirs’ discretion is paramount. The hadith mentions both qisas and diyah, but settlement is an independent option.
Thus, even a symbolic sum suffices to drop qisas in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسقط القود بموت القاتل، وبعفو الأولياء , ويصلحهم على مال قل أو جل. لقوله : فَمَنْ عُنِى لَهُ مِنْ أَخِيهِ شَيْءٌ ) الآية (٣) , على ما قيل : نزلت الآية في الصلح , وقوله الله : «من قتل له قتيل فأهله بين خيرتين إن شاؤوا أقادوا، وإن شاؤوا أخذوا الدية (4 ) والمراد الأخذ بالرضا على ما بين في موضعه ; ولأنه حق ثابت للورثة يجري فيه الإسقاط عفواً وكذا تعويضاً; لاشتماله على إحسان الأولياء وأحياء القاتل، فيجوز بالتراضي، والقليل والكثير فيه سواء ; لأنه ليس فيه نص مقدَّر
And qisas is dropped by the death of the killer, by the pardon of the legal heirs, and by their settlement on wealth, little or much. Because of His statement: 'But if anyone is granted something by his brother' [Quran 2:178], it is said the verse was revealed about settlement, and the Prophet's statement: 'Whoever has a killed person, his family has two choices: if they wish, they may exact qisas, and if they wish, they may take the blood-money.' And the intent is taking with satisfaction as explained in its place. And because it is a right established for the heirs, dropping by pardon or compensation is permissible; it includes kindness of the heirs and giving life to the killer, so it is permissible by mutual consent. Little and much are equal in it because there is no fixed text.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage outlines the three ways in which qisas for murder can be dropped: 1) the death of the killer, 2) the pardon of the legal heirs (awliya'), and 3) a settlement (sulh) on any amount of wealth, whether little or much. The proof is from the Quran (2:178) regarding pardon and settlement, and a hadith giving the heirs the choice between qisas and blood-money. The commentary explains that qisas is a right of the heirs, so they can drop it by pardon or accept compensation. The amount of compensation is not fixed by text, so it can be any mutually agreed sum. The Hanafi school allows settlement even for a small amount, as it encourages reconciliation and preserves life.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): Qisas for murder, i.e., the death penalty against the killer.
عفو الأولياء (afw al-awliya'): Pardon by the legal guardians (heirs) of the victim.
صلح (sulh): Settlement or compromise between the heirs and the killer on some compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qisas is a right of the heirs that can be dropped unconditionally and on any amount of compensation, as established by Quran, hadith, and the juristic principle of the heirs' discretionary authority.

Dropping of Qisas and Head Wound Compensation
Ruling on when qisas is dropped and head wound compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three causes for dropping qisas in Hanafi law and explain the victim's choice in asymmetric head wound cases.

Core Idea
Qisas is a right of the heirs — they may drop it by death, pardon, or any settlement amount.

This passage from Kitab al-Jinaayat establishes the foundational rules for when retaliatory execution (qisas) is no longer applicable. It identifies three specific causes — death of the killer, pardon by the heirs, and settlement on property — and clarifies that no fixed amount is required for settlement. The text also illustrates a practical scenario involving head wounds of different sizes, giving the victim the option between qisas and monetary compensation (arsh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three causes
Read the passage and list the three circumstances that cause qisas to be dropped: death of the killer, pardon by the heirs (awliya'), and settlement on property (sulh). Note that the settlement can be for any amount, little or much.
The term 'awliya' refers to the victim's legal heirs who hold the right to qisas.
2
Analyse the head wound scenario
Examine the specific example: the victim's head is small, so the wound covers the area between his temples; the perpetrator's head is large, so the same wound covers less relative area. The victim is given the choice to either exact qisas or take compensation (arsh). According to Al-Hidayah, the same choice applies in the opposite case (if the perpetrator's head is smaller).
The key point is that when exact retaliation is impossible or asymmetrical, monetary compensation becomes an option.
3
Locate the proof
The passage cites Quran 2:178 ('But whoever has something forgiven him by his brother') and a hadith ('Whoever has a slain person, his family is between two choices: if they wish, they may execute qisas, and if they wish, they may take the diyah'). Understand that these texts give the heirs the option to forgive or settle, indicating that qisas can be dropped by their choice.
The hadith is reported in Sunan al-Tirmidhi and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
4
Understand the legal principle
Qisas is a right of the heirs (haqq al-ibad), not a fixed penalty. Therefore, it can be waived or substituted by agreement. The lack of a specified amount for settlement shows that any amount is acceptable by mutual consent.
This distinguishes qisas from hudud punishments, which are rights of Allah and cannot be dropped.
5
Note the practical implication
The ruling applies broadly: settlement can be for a small amount (e.g., a goat) or large (full diyah). The heirs' choice is absolute, and no external authority can compel a specific amount.
Some other schools restrict settlement to the amount of diyah, but the Hanafi school permits any amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[1] قوله : والرأس المشجوج ... الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية» : وفي عكسه يُخَيَّرُ أيضاً ؛ لانه يتعدَّرُ الاستيفاء كملاً للتعدّي إلى غير حقه، وكذا إذا كانت الشجة في طول الرأس وهي تأخذ من جبهته إلى قفاه، ولا تبلغ إلى قفا الشاج، فهو بالخيار ؛ لأن المعنى لا يختلف.
(٢) قوله : ويسقط القود... الخ ؛ لقوله : فَمَنْ عُنِى لَهُ مِنْ أَخِيهِ شَيْءٌ ) الآية (٣) ، على ما قيل : نزلت الآية في الصلح ، وقوله الله : «من قتل له قتيل فأهله بين خيرتين إن شاؤوا أقادوا، وإن شاؤوا أخذوا الدية والمراد الأخذ بالرضا على ما بين في موضعه ؛ ولأنه حق ثابت للورثة يجري فيه الإسقاط عفواً وكذا تعويضاً؛ لاشتماله على إحسان الأولياء وأحياء القاتل، فيجوز بالتراضي، والقليل والكثير فيه سواء ؛ لأنه ليس فيه نص مقدَّر )
The Book of Crimes: Types of Killing and What Mandates Qisas and Testimony on It. Qisas is dropped by the death of the killer, by the pardon of the heirs (awliya'), and by their settlement for property, little or much. And the head of the injured person is small, so the head wound covers [the area] between his two temples, while the head of the perpetrator is large, so the wound does not cover [all of] his temples, being a handspan between his temples. Thus the handspan that befalls the injured is greater than what befalls the perpetrator. So the injured person has the choice: if he wishes, he may exact qisas, and if he wishes, he may take compensation (arsh). Qisas is dropped by the death of the killer, by the pardon of the heirs, and by their settlement for property, little or much. Except that if it is defective in attribute, the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he may take it defective, and if he wishes, he may revert to the value. The same applies here, so his right is dropped, just as if he was satisfied with inferior [goods] in place of good. [Commentary:] His saying: 'and the head of the injured person...' [etc.]; It is said in al-Hidayah: In the opposite case, he is also given a choice, because complete execution is impossible due to encroachment upon another's right. Similarly, if the wound is along the length of the head, extending from his forehead to the back of his head, and does not reach the back of the head of the perpetrator, then he has a choice, because the meaning does not differ. His saying: 'And qisas is dropped...' And the intended meaning is taking by consent, as explained in its place. And because it is a right established for the heirs in which dropping by pardon and likewise compensation is feasible, due to its inclusion of kindness to the heirs and sparing the killer's life, so it is permissible by mutual agreement, and the little and the much in it are equal, because there is no fixed text [for the amount].
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Jinaayat. It states that qisas (retaliatory killing) is dropped by three causes: (1) death of the killer, (2) pardon by the victim's heirs (awliya'), and (3) settlement on property (diyah or other), regardless of the amount (little or much). The text then gives a specific scenario regarding head wounds (shajjah): if the victim's head is small such that a wound covers the area between his temples, while the perpetrator's head is large so the same wound does not cover his temples, the victim has the choice to either exact qisas or take compensation (arsh). The same rule applies in the opposite case (if the perpetrator's head is smaller) according to Al-Hidayah. The proof is from the Quranic verse (2:178) which encourages settlement, and a hadith stating the family of the slain has the choice between qisas and diyah. The ruling emphasizes that settlement can be for any amount because there is no fixed text for it, and it is a right of the heirs that may be dropped or compensated by mutual agreement.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad (or al-qisas)): Retaliatory killing of the murderer as a legal punishment.
العفو (al-'afw): Pardon by the victim's heirs, which drops qisas without compensation.
الصلح (al-sulh): Settlement on property (diyah or other) in exchange for dropping qisas.
الشجة (al-shajjah): A head wound that reaches the bone or is severe.
الأرش (al-arsh): Monetary compensation for wounds where qisas is not applicable or chosen.

Key Takeaway
Qisas is a right of the heirs that may be dropped by death of the killer, their pardon, or any settlement, with no fixed amount — reflecting the principle of mutual consent.

The Effect of One Heir’s Settlement and Dispute on Spouses’ Inheritance in Qisas
Ruling on settlement by one heir and dispute on spouses' inheritance in qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that spouses inherit the right to qisas/diyah and evaluate the Maliki/Shafi‘i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A single heir’s settlement is effective; spouses are heirs in qisas despite death severing marriage.

This passage from Husn al-Diraya addresses two interconnected rulings: the validity of a settlement by one heir, binding on his share, and the dispute over whether spouses are among the heirs entitled to qisas and diyah. The Hanafi school uniquely includes spouses in these rights, contrary to Malik and al-Shafi‘i. We will unpack the proofs and the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on one heir's settlement
Identify the ruling: when one heir settles or pardons, the settlement is effective and the remaining heirs receive their share of diyah. The payment is immediate unless deferred is agreed.
The text emphasises that this applies according to us (Hanafis), setting up the dispute.
2
Identify the inter-madhhab dispute on spouses
Recognise that Malik and al-Shafi‘i exclude spouses from inheriting qisas and diyah. The Hanafi view includes them as heirs.
The key term 'zawjayn' (spouses) is the focus of the dispute.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Maliki/Shafi‘i argument: inheritance is based on lineage (nasab) not marriage (sabab), because marriage ends at death.
They consider qisas a personal right that does not pass through marriage.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal uses both transmission (hadith of the woman of Ashim) and reason (spouses inherit property by consensus, so qisas follows by qiyas).
The response is characterised as invalid (fāsid) by the opponents' own criteria.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, a spouse can pardon or settle qisas; under Maliki/Shafi‘i, the spouse has no such right, leaving the matter to blood relatives only.
This affects legal strategy in cases of homicide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حسن الدراية لأواخر شرح الوقاية
ويجب حالاً وبصلح أحدهم وبعفوه ، ولمن بقي حصته من الدية، فإن صالح بألف وكيل سيد عبد وحرّ قتلا فالصلح عن دمهما بألف بنصف ويجب حالاً) : أي إن لم يذكر الحلول والتأجيل يجب حالاً، ولا يكون كالدِّيةِ مؤجلاً ، ويصلح أحدهم ويعفوه ، ولمن بقي حصته من الدية) : أي من بقي من الورثة عندنا ، خلافا لمالك والشافعي ) في الزوجين.
[٢] فإن صالح بألف وكيل سيد عبد وحرّ قتلا فالصلح عن دمهما بألف بنصف) : أي إن كان القاتل حرَّاً وعبداً، فأمر الحر ومولى العبدِ رجلاً بأن يصالح من دمهما على ألف ففعل، فالألفُ على الحر والمولى نصفان. [ ١ ] قوله : ويجب حالاً ، لأنه مال واجب بالعقد، والأصل في أمثاله الحلول نحو المهر والثمن، بخلاف الدية ؛ لأنها ما وجبت بالعقد.
[٢] قوله : حق جميع الورثة ؛ فكل منهم يتمكن من الاستيفاء والإسقاط عفواً وصلحاً، ومن ضرورة سقوط حق البعض في القصاص سقوط حق الباقين فيه ؛ لأنه لا يتجزأ.
[٣] قوله : خلافا لمالك والشافعي في الزوجين ؛ لأنَّ الوراثة خلافة، وهي بالنسب دون السبب ؛ لانقطاعه بالموت، قُلنا : إنّه فاسد بالنقل والعقل ؛ أما الأول فبحديث امرأة أشيم، وأما الثاني ؛ فلأنهما موروثان كسائر الأموال بالاتفاق، فيجب أن يكون في حق الزوجين كذلك.
[٤]قوله : فإن صالح ؛ صورته : قتل الحر والعبد رجلاً، فأمر الحر ومولى العبد شخصاً بأن يصالح عن دم عليهما من ورثة المقتول على ألف درهم ففعل، فالألف على الحر ومولى العبد نصفان ؛ لأنَّ عقد الصلح أضيف إليهما ؛ لأنَّ الواجب بدل عن الدم، وكل واحد من الحر والمولى أضاف الصلح إلى نفسه.
Husn al-Diraya for the End of Sharh al-Wiqayah
And it is obligatory immediately (ḥālan) with the settlement of one of them and with his pardon, and for whoever remains, his share of the diyah. And if he settles for a thousand as a deputy of a master [of a slave] and a free man who were killed, then the settlement for their blood is for a thousand in halves. 'And it is obligatory immediately': meaning if he does not mention immediate payment or deferral, it is obligatory immediately, and it is not like the diyah that is deferred. 'And one of them may settle and pardon, and for whoever remains, his share of the diyah': meaning whoever remains of the heirs according to us, contrary to Malik and al-Shafi'i regarding the spouses (zawjayn). [2] Then if he settles for a thousand as a deputy of a master and a free man who are killed, then the settlement for their blood is for a thousand in halves: meaning if the killer is a free man and a slave, and the free man and the slave's master ordered a man to settle on their blood for a thousand, and he did so, then the thousand is between the free man and the master in halves. [1] His saying: 'And it is obligatory immediately', because it is property owed by contract, and the default in such cases is immediacy, like the dowry (mahr) and the price (thaman), unlike the diyah because it is not owed by contract. [2] His saying: 'It is the right of all the heirs' so each one of them has the power to execute and drop [the right] by pardon or settlement, and from the necessity of the dropping of the right of some in qisas is the dropping of the right of the rest in it, because it is indivisible. [3] His saying: 'Contrary to Malik and al-Shafi'i regarding the spouses', because inheritance is substitution (khilāfah), and it is by lineage (nasab) not by cause (sabab), because it is severed by death. We say: This is invalid by transmission and reason. As for the first, by the hadith of the woman of Ashim; as for the second, because they [spouses] inherit [from each other] like other properties by consensus, so it should be the same regarding the right of the spouses. [4] His saying: 'Then if he settles' : its scenario: a free man and a slave killed a man, and the free man and the master of the slave ordered a person to settle on the blood of the victim from his heirs for a thousand dirhams, and he did so, then the thousand is between the free man and the master in halves, because the contract of settlement was attributed to both of them, and because the obligatory [compensation] is a substitute for blood, and each of the free man and the master attributed the settlement to himself.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within a ruling. The matn states that if one heir settles or pardons, the settlement is effective, and the remaining heirs get their share of the diyah, with the obligation of payment being immediate unless deferred. The author comments that this is our (Hanafi) position, contrary to Malik and al-Shafi'i regarding spouses (i.e., whether spouses are among the heirs entitled to qisas/diyah). The Hanafi view holds that spouses are heirs in the right of qisas and diyah because they inherit from each other like other property. The opponent view (Malik/Shafi'i) argues that inheritance is by lineage (nasab) only, not by marriage (sabab), because marriage ends at death. The Hanafi refutes this with the hadith of the woman of Ashim (which shows spouses inherit) and rational argument that spouses mutually inherit by consensus, so qisas/diyah should follow. The passage also gives a scenario: if a free man and a slave kill someone, and the free man and the slave's master appoint a deputy to settle the blood for a thousand dirhams, the sum is split equally between the free man and the master because the contract is attributed to both.

Key Terms
صلح أحدهم (sulhu ahadihim): The settlement of one of the heirs with the killer for compensation, which is binding on his share.
الدية (al-diyah): The blood money paid in compensation for homicide or injury.
الزوجين (al-zawjayn): The spouses (husband and wife) of the deceased.
الوراثة خلافة (al-wirathatu khilafah): Inheritance is a form of substitution (of the heir for the deceased in rights).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when one heir settles with the killer, what happens to the remaining heirs' right?
A) They lose their right entirely
B) They receive their share of the diyah
C) They must also agree to the settlement
D) The settlement is invalid

Key Takeaway
Spouses inherit the right to qisas/diyah in the Hanafi school, and one heir's settlement does not extinguish the others' shares in diyah.
